وفي تعريف الجزئي الإضافي نظر ، لأنه والكلّي الإضافي متضايفان، لأن معني الجزئي الإضافي الخاص ومعني الكلي الإضافي العام، وكما أن الإضافي ما أمكن اندراج شيء تحته، فيكون أيضاً أخص من الكلّي الحقيقي، لكن بدرجة واحدة، ولا يصح أن يقال : «الجزئي الإضافي ما أمكن فرض اندراجه تحت شيء آخر حتى يلزم أنّ الكلّي الإضافي ما أمكن فرض اندراج شيء تحته، فيرجع إلى المعنى الحقيقي كمامر. وإنما لم يصح تفسير الجزئي الإضافي بما ذكرنا لأنه لا يقال للفرس «إنه جزئي إضافي للإنسان» مع إمكان فرض الاندراج.فتأمل ليتضح لك أن الحق أن الكلي أيضاً له مفهومان : أحدهما حقيقي يقابل مفهوم الجزئي الحقيقي تقابل العدم للملكة، وليس توقف تعقله على تعقل الغير مستلزماً لكونه إضافياً كما في الجزئي الحقيقي بعينه على ما عرفت. وثانيهما إضافي يقابل الجزئي الإضافي تقابل التضايف، وأن الحال بين الكليين في النسبة عكس ما بين الجزئيين، فالكلّي الإضافي أخص من الحقيقي كمامر، والجزئي الإضافي أعم من الحقيقي كما سنبينه (شريف). (۱) وذلك لما عرفت أن معنى الجزئي الإضافي هو المندرج تحت غيره، وهذا هو معنى الخاص بعينه، ومعنى الكلي الإضافي هو المندرج تحته شيء آخر، وهذا هو معنى العام بعينه فالخاص والجزئي الإضافي بمعنى واحد، وكذلك العام والكلّي الإضافي بمعنى واحد، ولاشك أن الخاص والعام متضايفان مشهوران كالأب والابن وأن الخصوص والعموم متضايفان حقيقيان كالأبوة والبنوة، والمتضايفان لا يعقلان إلا معا ، فلا يجوز أن يذكر أحدهما في تعريف الآخر، وإلا لكان تعقله قبل تعقله، ضرورة أن تعقل المعرف وأجزائه مقدم على تعقل المعرف. فإن قلت: المذكور في تعريف الجزئي الإضافي هو الأعم لا العام الذي هو بمعنى الكلّى الإضافي حتى يلزم ذكر أحد المتضايفين في تعريف الآخر الخاص خاص بالنسبة إلى العام، كذلك العام عام بالنسبة إلى الخاص وأحد المتضايفين لا يجوز أن يذكر في تعريف المتضايف الآخر، وإلا لكان تعقله قبل تعقله - لامعه - وأيضاً لفظة «كلّ» إنما هي للأفراد والتعريف بالأفراد ليس بجائز، فالأولى أن يقال هو الأخص من شيء. قلت: تعقل الأعمّ يتوقف على تعقل العام، الذي هو الإضافي مع أن المقصود بالأعم والأخص هاهنا هو العام والخاص، لا معنى التفضيل والزيادة في العموم والخصوص، لكن على هذا يلزم تعريف الجزئي الإضافي بالخاص الذي هو بمعناه، فيلزم تعريف الشيء بنفسه ومضايفه معاً ؛ وعلى الأول يلزم تعريفه بالأخص الذي يتوقف تعقله على تعقل الخاص، فيلزم تعريف الشيء بما يتوقف معرفته على معرفته وبما يتوقف على معرفة مضايفه، فالخلل في التعريف من وجهين : أحدهما تعريف الشيء بنفسه أو بما يتوقف على معرفته، والثاني تعريفه بمضايفه أو بما يتوقف على معرفة مضايفه ؛ ولاشك أن الخلل الأول أقوى من الثاني، فالأولى أن لا يقتصر على الثاني وحده. وأيضاً يلزم أن لا يكون تعريفه بالأخص من شيء - كما ذكره الشارح - صحيحاً لاشتماله على الخلل الأول قطعاً - هذا. وقد قيل في جواب النظر : إنّ المصنف ذكر المتضايفين معاً - أعني الأخص والأعم - في تعريف شيء واحد هو الجزئي الإضافي، ولا محذور في ذلك». وليس بشيء : لأن هذا القائل إن سلّم أن معنى الجزئي الإضافي هو الخاص ومعنى الكلّي الإضافي هو العام - كما ذكره الشارح - : فالنظر وارد مع زيادة كما عرفت؛ وإن لم يسلم : فالجواب هو ذاك، لا ما ذكره. ومنهم من قال: لم يرد المصنف بما ذكره تعريف الجزئي الإضافي، بل أراد ذكر حكم من أحكامه يمكن أن يستنبط منه له تعريف، وحينئذ يندفع الاشكالان معاً، إلا أن المقام يدلّ على قصد التعريف ظاهراً (شريف).
There is an objection in the definition of the partial by relation (al-juz'i al-idafi), because it and the universal by relation (al-kulli al-idafi) are correlatives, since the meaning of the partial by relation is the specific (al-khass) and the meaning of the universal by relation is the general (al-'amm). And just as the by-relation (al-idafi) is that which it is possible for something to be subsumed under it, thus it is also more specific than the real universal (al-kulli al-haqiqi), but by one degree. And it is not correct to say: 'The partial by relation is that which it is possible to suppose its subsumption under something else,' because then it would follow that the universal by relation is that which it is possible to suppose the subsumption of something under it, thus it would revert to the real meaning as before. And the interpretation of the partial by relation as what we mentioned is not correct because one does not say of a horse, 'It is a partial by relation to man,' despite the possibility of supposing subsumption. So reflect so that it becomes clear to you that the truth is that the universal (al-kulli) also has two concepts: one is real, corresponding to the concept of the real partial (al-juz'i al-haqiqi) in the correspondence of privation to possession, and its conception not being dependent on conceiving another does not entail its being by relation, just as in the real partial exactly, as you have understood. And the second is by relation (idafi), corresponding to the partial by relation in the correspondence of correlation. And the situation between the two universals in respect to relation is the reverse of that between the two partials. So the universal by relation is more specific than the real universal, as before, and the partial by relation is more general than the real partial, as we will explain. That is because you know that the meaning of the partial by relation is that which is subsumed under something else, and this is exactly the meaning of the specific (al-khass); and the meaning of the universal by relation is that under which something else is subsumed, and this is exactly the meaning of the general (al-'amm). So the specific and the partial by relation are synonymous, and likewise the general and the universal by relation are synonymous. And there is no doubt that the specific and the general are well-known correlatives like father and son, and that specificity and generality are real correlatives like fatherhood and sonship. And correlatives are not conceived except together, so it is not permissible to mention one of them in the definition of the other; otherwise, its conception would be before its conception, necessarily because the conception of the definiendum and its parts is prior to the conception of the definiendum. If you say: What is mentioned in the definition of the partial by relation is the more general (al-a'mm), not the general (al-'amm) which is synonymous with the universal by relation, so that it would entail mentioning one of the correlatives in the definition of the other. The specific is specific in relation to the general, and likewise the general is general in relation to the specific. And one of the correlatives is not permissible to be mentioned in the definition of the other correlative; otherwise, its conception would be before its conception — without it. Also, the word 'every' (kull) is only for individuals, and definition by individuals is not permissible. So it is better to say: It is the more specific than something. I say: The conception of the more general (al-a'mm) depends on the conception of the general (al-'amm), which is the by-relation, although the intended meaning here by 'more general' and 'more specific' is the general and the specific, not the meaning of superiority and increase in generality and specificity. But on this, it would entail defining the partial by relation by the specific (al-khass), which is its synonym, thus entailing defining the thing by itself and its correlative together. And on the first view, it entails defining it by the more specific (al-akhass), whose conception depends on the conception of the specific, thus entailing defining the thing by that which its knowledge depends on its knowledge, and by that which depends on the knowledge of its correlative. So the defect in the definition is from two aspects: one is defining the thing by itself or by that which depends on its knowledge; the second is defining it by its correlative or by that which depends on knowledge of its correlative. And there is no doubt that the first defect is stronger than the second, so it is better not to confine oneself to the second alone. Also, it would entail that the definition by 'the more specific than something' — as the commentator (al-Sharh) mentioned — is not correct, because it includes the first defect necessarily. This is it. And it has been said in answer to the objection: The author (al-Musannif) mentioned the two correlatives together — i.e., the more specific and the more general — in the definition of one thing, which is the partial by relation, and there is no harm in that. But this is nothing, because if this proponent concedes that the meaning of the partial by relation is the specific and the meaning of the universal by relation is the general — as the commentator mentioned — then the objection is valid with an addition, as you know; and if he does not concede, then the answer is that, not what he mentioned. And among them is he who said: The author did not intend by what he mentioned a definition of the partial by relation; rather, he intended to mention one of its rulings from which a definition for it can be derived. In that case, both problems are repelled, except that the context indicates the intent of definition apparently.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the definition of 'the partial by relation' (al-juz'i al-idafi). The author begins by stating that there is an objection (nazar) in its definition, because al-juz'i al-idafi and al-kulli al-idafi (the universal by relation) are correlatives (mutada'ifan). The meaning of al-juz'i al-idafi is the specific (al-khass), and al-kulli al-idafi is the general (al-'amm). The author explains that 'by relation' means that it is possible for something to be subsumed under it. Thus, al-juz'i al-idafi is more specific than the real universal (al-kulli al-haqiqi) by one degree. The common definition 'that which can be supposed to be subsumed under something else' is criticized because it would make al-kulli al-idafi 'that under which something is subsumed,' which is the real meaning. Moreover, we do not call a horse 'partial by relation to man' even though it could be subsumed under man, showing the definition fails. The author then states that the universal has two concepts: real (haqiqi) and by relation (idafi). The real universal corresponds to the real partial, and its conception does not depend on conceiving another. The by-relation universal corresponds to the partial by relation. The relation between the two universals is the reverse of that between the two partials: the universal by relation is more specific than the real universal, while the partial by relation is more general than the real partial. The reason is that al-juz'i al-idafi means 'that which is subsumed under something else,' which is exactly the specific; al-kulli al-idafi means 'that under which something else is subsumed,' which is exactly the general. Thus, the specific and the partial by relation are synonymous, and the general and the universal by relation are synonymous. Since the specific and the general are correlatives, they cannot be conceived separately; hence, one cannot be used in defining the other, as that would require prior conception of the definiendum. An objection is raised: In the definition of al-juz'i al-idafi, the term used is 'the more general' (al-a'mm), not 'the general' (al-'amm), so no direct mention of the correlative occurs. Also, the word 'kull' restricts to individuals, which is not permissible in definitions. A better definition would be 'the more specific than something' (al-akhass min shay'). The author responds that conceiving 'the more general' depends on conceiving 'the general,' which is the correlative. Here, 'more general' and 'more specific' mean the general and the specific, not comparative superiority. This leads to defining al-juz'i al-idafi by the specific, which is its synonym, causing self-definition and definition by a correlative. Thus, the definition suffers two defects: defining by itself or something that depends on its own knowledge, and defining by its correlative or something dependent on the correlative's knowledge. The first defect is stronger. Therefore, the suggested definition by 'the more specific than something' is also flawed. Some argue that the author mentioned both correlatives together, but this is rejected because if one accepts that al-juz'i al-idafi equals the specific, the objection stands; if not, the answer is different. Another response says the author intended to mention a property, not a definition, but the context suggests otherwise. The passage is a classic example of the rigor in defining logical terms and the pitfalls of circularity and correlative definitions.

الكلي الإضافي

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is defining al-juz'i al-idafi as 'al-akhass min shay' (the more specific than something) problematic?
A) It uses the word 'kull' which is only for individuals.
B) It defines the term by its correlative indirectly, and also leads to self-definition.
C) It is too vague to be useful.
D) It fails to distinguish it from the real universal.

Key Takeaway
Defining a correlative term requires careful avoidance of circularity, either by avoiding the correlative entirely or by defining both together as a pair.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'The general (al-'amm) is that which applies to more than one individual.' Is this a valid definition? Identify any logical issues using the criteria from this lesson.
?
In a debate, someone defines 'the specific' (al-khass) as 'the opposite of the general.' Explain why this definition is problematic based on the critique of correlatives.

The Four Ranks of Genera
Defining the four ranks of genera with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and exemplify each of the four ranks of genera (higher, lower, intermediate, isolated) as defined in the passage.

Core Idea
Genera have four ranks: higher, lower, intermediate, and isolated.

In this lesson, we will explore the four ranks of genera from the tradition of Islamic logic. Just as species are arranged in a descending order, genera are arranged in an ascending order. We will learn to distinguish each rank with its defining property and examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the higher genus (الجنس العالي)
Find the genus that has no genus above it; the most universal genus. The passage gives 'substance' (الجوهر) as an example.
2
Identify the lower genus (الجنس السافل)
Find the genus that has no species below it; the least universal genus. The passage gives 'animal' (الحيوان) as an example.
3
Identify the intermediate genus (الجنس المتوسط)
Find a genus that is both more universal and more specific than others; it sits in a chain. Examples given: 'growing body' (الجسم النامي) and 'body' (الجسم).
4
Identify the isolated genus (الجنس المفرد)
Find a genus that is distinct from all others, with no genus above or below. The passage mentions 'intellect' (العقل) if substance is not its genus.
Some scholars exclude this rank.

قال : ومراتب الأجناس أيضاً هذه الأربع : لأنه إن كان أعم الأجناس فهو «الجنس العالي» كالجوهر. وإن كان أخصها فهو «الجنس السافل» كالحيوان. أو أعم وأخص فهو «الجنس المتوسط» كالجسم النامي والجسم. أو مبايناً للكل فهو «الجنس المفرد». القول : كما أن الأنواع الإضافية قد تترتب متنازلة كذلك الأجناس أيضاً قد تترتب متصاعدة حتى يكون جنس فوقه جنس آخر ؛ وكما أن (١) هذا المثال إنما يتم بشيئين : أحدهما أنّ العقول العشرة متفقة بالحقيقة، وثانيهما أن الجوهر جنس لها (شريف). (٢) أشار بلفظة «قد» إلى أن الترتب في الأجناس مما لا يجب كما لا يجب في الأنواع أيضاً، فكما يكون نوع إضافي لا نوع فوقه ولا نوع تحته فيكون نوعاً مفرداً غير واقع في سلسلة الترتب كذلك يكون جنس لا جنس فوقه ولا تحته فيكون جنساً مفرداً وليس واقعاً في سلسلة الترتّب، فمثل هذا ينبغي أن لا يعد من المراتب و تجعل المراتب منحصرة في ثلاثة - كما فعله بعضهم - إلا أنهم تسامحوا فعدوه من المراتب نظراً إلى ما ذكرنا من أن اعتبار إفراده يحوج إلى ملاحظة الترتب عدماً. و إنما قال في الأنواع «متنازلة» وفي الأجناس «متصاعدة» لأن ترتب الأنواع هو أن يكون هناك نوع و نوع نوع و نوع نوع النوع؛ ولاشك أن نوع النوع يكون تحته، لأن نوعية الشيء بالقياس إلى ما فوقه، فالشيء إنما يكون «نوع نوع» إذا كان تحت ذلك النوع - وهكذا – فيكون الترتيب على سبيل التنازل من عام إلى خاص. وترتب الأجناس هو أن يثبت جنس و جنس جنس و جنس جنس الجنس، ولا شك أن جنس الجنس يكون فوقه لأن جنسية الشيء بالقياس إلى ما تحته، فالشيء إنما يكون جنس جنس إذا كان فوق ذلك الجنس - وهكذا - فيكون الترتب على سبيل التصاعد من خاص إلى عام. ثم اعلم أن النوع السافل من مراتب الأنواع مباين جميع مراتب الأجناس، فإنه لا يكون إلا نوعاً حقيقياً، فيستحيل أن يكون جنساً، وأن الجنس العالي يباين جميع مراتب الأنواع، لأنه لا يكون فوقه جنس، فيستحيل أن يكون نوعاً، وبين كلّ واحد من النوع العالي والمتوسط وبين كل واحد من المتوسط والسافل عموم من وجه؛ وعليك باستخراج الأمثلة (شريف).
He said: And the ranks of genera are also these four: because if it is the most universal of genera, then it is the 'higher genus', like substance. And if it is the most specific, then it is the 'lower genus', like animal. Or [if it is] both more universal and more specific, then it is the 'intermediate genus', like the growing body and body. Or [if it is] distinct from all, then it is the 'isolated genus'. The statement: Just as relative species may be arranged descending, likewise genera also may be arranged ascending, such that a genus has another genus above it. And just as (1) this example is only completed by two things: one is that the ten intellects are identical in reality, and the second is that substance is a genus for them (Sharif). (2) He indicated by the word 'may' that the arrangement in genera is not necessary, just as it is also not necessary in species. For just as there is a relative species with no species above it and no species below it, so it is an isolated species not occurring in the chain of arrangement, likewise there is a genus with no genus above it and no genus below it, so it is an isolated genus and not occurring in the chain of arrangement. So such [a genus] should not be counted among the ranks, and the ranks should be restricted to three — as some have done — except that they were lenient and counted it among the ranks, considering what we mentioned that taking into account its isolation necessitates noting the arrangement in terms of non-existence. And he only said in species 'descending' and in genera 'ascending' because the arrangement of species is that there is a species, and a species of a species, and a species of a species of a species. And there is no doubt that the species of a species is below it, because the species-ness of a thing is relative to what is above it. Thus a thing is only a 'species of a species' if it is under that species — and so on — so the arrangement is descending from general to specific. And the arrangement of genera is that there is a genus, and a genus of a genus, and a genus of a genus of a genus. And there is no doubt that the genus of a genus is above it, because the genus-ness of a thing is relative to what is below it. Thus a thing is only a 'genus of a genus' if it is above that genus — and so on — so the arrangement is ascending from specific to general. Then know that the lower species from the ranks of species is distinct from all the ranks of genera, for it is only a true species, so it is impossible for it to be a genus. And the higher genus is distinct from all the ranks of species, because there is no genus above it, so it is impossible for it to be a species. And between each of the higher and intermediate species and each of the intermediate and lower [genera] there is a generality from one perspective. And it is upon you to extract the examples (Sharif).
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the four ranks of genera in Ilm al-Mantiq. The author begins by stating that genera also have four ranks, analogous to the four ranks of species. These are: (1) the higher genus (الجنس العالي), which is the most universal genus with no genus above it, exemplified by الجوهر (substance). (2) The lower genus (الجنس السافل), which is the most specific genus with no species below it, exemplified by الحيوان (animal). (3) The intermediate genus (الجنس المتوسط), which is both more universal and more specific than some other genera, exemplified by الجسم النامي (growing body) and الجسم (body). (4) The isolated genus (الجنس المفرد), which is distinct from all others, neither above nor below any other genus, exemplified by العقل (intellect) if substance is not its genus. The commentary then discusses the descending arrangement of species versus the ascending arrangement of genera. For species, the chain goes from general to specific (type, subtype, sub-subtype), hence 'descending'. For genera, it goes from specific to general (genus, supergenus, super-supergenus), hence 'ascending'. The passage also notes that the arrangement is not necessary—there can be isolated genera not fitting into a chain. Some scholars limit the ranks to three, excluding the isolated case, but the author considers it a rank due to the logical consideration of isolation. Finally, the relationship between species and genera is clarified: the lowest species (نوع سافل) is a true species and cannot be a genus, while the highest genus (جنس عالي) cannot be a species. There is a partial generality (عموم من وجه) between certain ranks, and the reader is tasked with finding examples.

Key Terms
الجنس العالي
الجنس السافل
الجنس المتوسط
الجنس المفرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of an intermediate genus?
A) الجوهر (substance)
B) الحيوان (animal)
C) الجسم النامي (growing body)
D) العقل (intellect)

Key Takeaway
Genera are classified into four ranks based on their universality: higher, lower, intermediate, and isolated.

Ascending vs Descending and the Isolated Genus Debate
Expanding on ascending/descending arrangement and the isolated genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why genera are arranged ascendingly while species descend, and evaluate the inclusion of the isolated genus as a rank.

Core Idea
Species descend, genera ascend; the isolated genus sparks a debate on rank counting.

This lesson delves into the commentary's explanation of the ascending arrangement of genera versus the descending arrangement of species. We will also examine the controversy over whether the isolated genus should be counted as a separate rank, a point some scholars dispute.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the ascending vs descending metaphor
Genera are arranged from specific to general: a genus, a genus of a genus, etc. This is ascending because the higher genus is above. Species are arranged from general to specific: a species, a species of a species, descending.
The commentary emphasizes this contrast using the words 'متنازلة' (descending) and 'متصاعدة' (ascending).
2
Understand the reason for the direction
For species, each lower level is a 'species of a species' (underneath). For genera, each higher level is a 'genus of a genus' (above). This is due to the relation of genus-ness to what is below and species-ness to what is above.
3
Analyze the isolated genus discussion
The commentary notes that some scholars exclude the isolated genus from the ranks because it does not fit in a chain. The author, however, includes it by considering its isolation as a special case.
The passage uses the word 'قد' (may) to indicate that arrangement is not necessary.
4
Relate lowest species and highest genus
The lowest species is a true species and cannot be a genus; the highest genus is a true genus and cannot be a species. There is partial generality between other ranks.
The reader is tasked with finding examples, showing an active learning component.

The Four Ranks of Genera: Classification and Exclusion
Author defines the four ranks of genera.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any genus into one of the four ranks and explain why some scholars exclude the isolated genus.

Core Idea
Genera form a hierarchy of four ranks, but the isolated genus is a borderline case.

This passage introduces the four ranks of genera in the Porphyrian tree, a key tool for defining terms in Islamic logic. Understanding these ranks helps you evaluate definitions in kalam and fiqh. We'll walk through each rank and the debate over whether the isolated genus should be counted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the high genus
Look for the term that is the most general, having no genus above it. The author gives 'substance' (jawhar) as an example.
High genus is at the top of the tree.
2
Identify the low genus
Find the most specific genus, which has no genus below it but is still a genus for species. Example: 'animal' (hayawan).
Low genus is the lowest genus before species.
3
Identify the intermediate genus
This genus is both a genus (for lower items) and a species (for higher items). Example: 'body' (jism) – more general than animal, more specific than substance.
Intermediate genera form a chain.
4
Identify the isolated genus
This genus does not fall into a continuous chain of subordination; it stands alone. The isolated genus is not truly a rank in the hierarchy.
Some scholars omit it from the ranks.
5
Evaluate the dispute
Note that the author mentions some scholars limit the ranks to three, excluding the isolated genus. Understand both positions.
The author shows leniency but implies the strict view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مراتب الأنواع أربع فكذلك مراتب الأجناس أيضاً تلك الأربع : لأنه إن كان أعم الأجناس فهو «الجنس العالي» كالجوهر. وإن كان أخصها فهو «الجنس السافل» كالحيوان. أو أعم وأخص فهو «الجنس المتوسط» كالجسم النامي والجسم. أو مبايناً للكل فهو «الجنس المفرد». جنساً مفرداً وليس واقعاً في سلسلة الترتّب، فمثل هذا ينبغي أن لا يعد من المراتب و تجعل المراتب منحصرة في ثلاثة - كما فعله بعضهم - إلا أنهم تسامحوا فعدوه من المراتب نظراً إلى ما ذكرنا من أن اعتبار إفراده يحوج إلى ملاحظة الترتب عدماً.
The ranks of species are four, and likewise the ranks of genera are also those four: because if it is the most general of genera, it is the 'high genus' like jawhar (substance). If it is the most specific, it is the 'low genus' like hayawan (animal). Or it is more general and more specific, so it is the 'intermediate genus' like jism namī (growing body) and jism (body). Or it is distinct from all, so it is the 'isolated genus'. It is an isolated genus and does not fall into the chain of ordering, so such should not be counted among the ranks and the ranks should be limited to three – as some have done – except that they were lenient and counted it among the ranks in view of what we mentioned: that considering it isolated necessitates observing the ordering non-existently.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage defines the four ranks of genera in the Porphyrian tree: high genus (e.g., substance), low genus (e.g., animal), intermediate genus (e.g., body), and isolated genus (e.g., intellect on one interpretation). The isolated genus does not fit into a continuous series of subordination, so some scholars restrict the ranks to three. The author justifies the inclusion of the isolated genus by noting that its isolation is understood in relation to the ordering, albeit negatively.

Why Species Descend and Genera Ascend
Author explains why species descend and genera ascend.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why species are described as descending and genera as ascending in the Porphyrian tree.

Core Idea
Species are defined by what is above; genera are defined by what is below.

Species and genera are not ordered in the same direction. This lesson unpacks the relational logic behind the Porphyrian tree: why species descend from general to specific, while genera ascend from specific to general. The key lies in how each term relates to what is above or below it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two relational terms
The passage defines 'naw' naw'' (species of a species) and 'jins jins' (genus of a genus). Notice the different relational phrases: 'under that species' for species, and 'above that genus' for genera.
2
Understand the directional basis
Species-ness is relative to what is above: a species is defined by its higher genus. So 'species of a species' must be below. Genus-ness is relative to what is below: a genus is defined by its lower species. So 'genus of a genus' must be above.
This is the core logical insight.
3
Apply to a concrete chain
Consider: substance (genus) → body (species of substance) → human (species of body). Human is 'species species' relative to substance; it descends. Conversely, substance is 'genus genus' relative to human; it ascends.
Each step changes the direction.
4
Summarise the rule
The ordering direction depends on the type of relativity: species are ordered descending (general to specific), genera are ordered ascending (specific to general). This matches the passage's explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قال في الأنواع «متنازلة» وفي الأجناس «متصاعدة» لأن ترتب الأنواع هو أن يكون هناك نوع» و «نوع نوع» و«نوع نوع النوع»؛ ولاشك أن نوع النوع يكون تحته، لأن نوعية الشيء بالقياس إلى مافوقه، فالشيء إنما يكون «نوع نوع» إذا كان تحت ذلك النوع - وهكذا – فيكون الترتيب على سبيل التنازل من عام إلى خاص. وترتب الأجناس هو أن يثبت «جنس» و «جنس جنس» و «جنس جنس الجنس»، ولا شك أن «جنس الجنس» يكون فوقه لأن جنسية الشيء بالقياس إلى ما تحته، فالشيء إنما يكون جنس جنس» إذا كان فوق ذلك الجنس - وهكذا - فيكون الترتب على سبيل التصاعد من خاص إلى عام.
He said regarding species 'descending' and regarding genera 'ascending' because the ordering of species is that there is a species, and a species of a species, and a species of a species of a species; and there is no doubt that the species of a species is below it, because the species-ness of a thing is relative to what is above it, so a thing is a 'species of a species' only if it is under that species – and so on – so the ordering is in the manner of descending from general to specific. And the ordering of genera is that there is a genus, and a genus of a genus, and a genus of a genus of a genus; and there is no doubt that the genus of a genus is above it because the genus-ness of a thing is relative to what is below it, so a thing is a 'genus of a genus' only if it is above that genus – and so on – so the ordering is in the manner of ascending from specific to general.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage explains why species are described as descending and genera as ascending in the Porphyrian tree. The reason lies in the relative nature of species and genus: a species is defined by what is above it, so when we say 'species of a species', the second species is under the first, making the order go downward. Conversely, a genus is defined by what is below it, so 'genus of a genus' places the second genus above the first, making the order go upward. This clarifies the different directions of the tree.

Key Terms
نوع نوع
جنس جنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a 'species of a species' (نوع نوع) below the original species?
A) Because species-ness is relative to what is below it
B) Because species-ness is relative to what is above it
C) Because the species of a species is always a genus
D) Because the ordering is ascending

Key Takeaway
Species are ordered descending (general to specific) because their definition references what is above; genera are ordered ascending (specific to general) because their definition references what is below.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Ranks of Genera and Species
Defines the ranks of genera and species and their relationships.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the highest genus (جنس الأجناس) from the lowest species (نوع الأنواع) and identify the 'عموم من وجه' relationship between intermediate ranks.

Core Idea
The highest genus cannot be a species, and the lowest species cannot be a genus; they are distinct extremes.

In this passage, the author defines the distinctive properties of the highest genus and the lowest species, and explains the 'عموم من وجه' relationship that holds between intermediate ranks. Understanding these relationships is fundamental to mastering the hierarchy of universals in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the highest genus and lowest species
Read the first sentence. The author says the lowest species is distinct from all genera, and the highest genus is distinct from all species. Note that they are mutually exclusive.
The highest genus is jins al-ajnas, the lowest species is naw' al-anwa'.
2
Understand the 'عموم من وجه' relationship
The author states that between high and intermediate species, and between intermediate and low species, there is a general-specific relationship (عموم من وجه). This means they share some instances but not all.
For example, in the hierarchy of created beings, 'living' and 'knowing' may have عموم من وجه.
3
Learn the naming convention
The highest genus is called 'جنس الأجناس' because its genus-ness is relative to what is below it. The lowest species is called 'نوع الأنواع' because its species-ness is relative to what is above it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن النوع السافل من مراتب الأنواع مباين جميع مراتب الأجناس، فإنه لا يكون إلا نوعاً حقيقياً، فيستحيل أن يكون جنساً، وأن الجنس العالي يباين جميع مراتب الأنواع، لأنه لا يكون فوقه جنس، فيستحيل أن يكون نوعاً، وبين كلّ واحد من النوع العالي والمتوسط وبين كل واحد من المتوسط والسافل عموم من وجه؛ وعليك باستخراج الأمثلة (شريف). إلا أن العالي في مراتب الأجناس يسمّى «جنس الأجناس» لا السافل، والسافل في مراتب الأنواع يسمّى «نوع الأنواع»- لا العالي - وذلك لأنّ جنسية الشيء إنما هي بالقياس إلى ماتحته، فهو إنما يكون جنس الأجناس إذا كان فوق جميع الأجناس، ونوعية الشيء إنما تكون بالقياس إلى مافوقه، فهو إنما يكون نوع الأنواع إذا كان تحت جميع الأنواع. والجنس المفرد ممثل بالعقل على تقدير أن لا يكون الجوهر جنساً له، فإنّه ليس أعم من جنس - إذ ليس تحته إلا العقول العشرة، وهي أنواع لا أجناس - ولا أخص إذ ليس فوقه إلا الجوهر، وقد فرض أنه ليس بجنس له. (۱ لا يقال : أحد التمثيلين فاسد ؛ إما تمثيل النوع المفرد بالعقل على تقدير جنسية الجوهر؛ و إما تمثيل الجنس المفرد بالعقل على تقدير عرضية الجوهر، لأن العقل إن كان جنساً يكون تحته أنواع فلايكون نوعاً مفرداً، بل كان عالياً ، فلا يصح التمثيل الأول ، وإن لم يكن جنساً لم يصح التمثيل الثاني ضرورة أن ما لا يكون جنساً لا يكون جنساً مفرداً. لأنا نقول : التمثيل الأول على تقدير أن العقول العشرة متفقة بالنوع. (۱ قد عرفت أن تمثيل الأول مبني على اتفاق العقول العشرة في الحقيقة وكون الجوهر جنساً لها، والتمثيل الثاني موقوف على اختلافها في الحقيقة وكون الجوهر ليس جنساً لها، فيستحيل صحتهما معا. ف والا والجواب : أن المقصود من التمثيل هو التفهيم، فإن طابق الواقع فذاك، لم يضر ، إذ يكفيه مجرد الفرض - خصوصا فيما لم يوجد له مثال في الوجود ظاهراً (شريف).
Then know that the lowest species among the ranks of species is distinct from all the ranks of genera, for it is only a true species, so it is impossible for it to be a genus. And the highest genus is distinct from all the ranks of species, because there is no genus above it, so it is impossible for it to be a species. And between each of the high and intermediate species and each of the intermediate and low species there is a general-specific relationship (عموم من وجه); you must extract examples (Sharif). Except that the highest among the ranks of genera is called 'genus of genera' not the lowest, and the lowest among the ranks of species is called 'species of species' not the highest. And that is because the genus-ness of a thing is only relative to what is below it, so it is only a genus of genera if it is above all genera; and the species-ness of a thing is only relative to what is above it, so it is only a species of species if it is under all species. And the isolated genus is exemplified by the intellect ('aql) on the assumption that substance (jawhar) is not a genus for it. For it is not more general than a genus – since there is nothing under it except the ten intellects, which are species, not genera – nor more specific, since there is nothing above it except substance, and it has been assumed that it is not a genus for it. (One cannot say: One of the two examples is corrupt: either the example of the isolated species by the intellect on the assumption of substance being a genus, or the example of the isolated genus by the intellect on the assumption of substance being an accident; because if the intellect is a genus, then species are under it, so it is not an isolated species, but rather a high one; thus the first example is invalid. And if it is not a genus, then the second example is invalid necessarily, since what is not a genus is not an isolated genus. For we say: The first example is on the assumption that the ten intellects agree in species. (You have known that the first example is based on the agreement of the ten intellects in essence and substance being a genus for them, and the second example depends on their difference in essence and substance not being a genus for them, so it is impossible for both to be true.) Then the answer: The purpose of the example is to clarify; if it matches reality, that is fine; otherwise it does no harm, because mere assumption suffices – especially in what has no example apparent in existence (Sharif).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage covers the distinctive properties of the highest genus and lowest species, the names 'genus of genera' and 'species of species', and then presents a dialectical exchange about the example of the isolated genus. The objection argues that the two examples (isolated species and isolated genus) given previously are contradictory because they rely on opposite assumptions about the intellect. The answer defends the examples by stating their purpose is pedagogical; they are hypothetical and need not be simultaneously true. The author emphasizes that mere assumption suffices, especially for concepts with no obvious real-world instance.

Key Terms
جنس الأجناس
نوع الأنواع
عموم من وجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The highest genus and lowest species are mutually exclusive; the names reflect their position in the hierarchy relative to what is above or below.

The Isolated Genus: Example and Dialectical Exchange
Presents the isolated genus example and a dialectical exchange over its consistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection against the isolated genus example and explain the author's defense using the purpose of clarification.

Core Idea
The isolated genus example is hypothetical and serves pedagogical clarity, not factual accuracy.

This passage presents a dialectical exchange: an objection points out an apparent contradiction in the examples of the isolated genus and isolated species. The author responds by clarifying that the examples are for illustration only, and hypothetical assumptions are sufficient. This teaches us how to defend logical examples that may not have real-world counterparts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the isolated genus example
The author gives the intellect ('aql) as an example of an isolated genus, assuming that substance is not its genus. This means the intellect has no genus above it and no species below it except the ten intellects, which are species, not genera, so it is not more general than a genus. And nothing above it except substance, which is assumed not to be its genus.
2
Identify the objection
The objector says one of the two examples (isolated species and isolated genus) must be corrupt because they rely on opposite assumptions about the intellect's relationship to substance.
The two examples were likely given earlier in the text.
3
Analyze the answer
The author responds by stating that the examples are for clarification; even if they do not match reality, the assumption suffices. He adds that this is especially relevant when no real-world example is apparent.

Direct vs. Implied Indication in Definitions
Author distinguishes between direct and implied indication in answering 'what is it?'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between direct (mutabaqa) and implied (tadammun) indication in definitions and identify which terms are valid as direct answers to 'what is it?'.

Core Idea
The essence is only revealed by the definition that directly corresponds, not by its implied parts.

This passage from al-Qutbi clarifies a crucial distinction in definition: when we answer 'what is it?' for a thing, only those terms that directly indicate the quiddity by mutabaqa are proper answers. Terms that are implied (tadammun) are parts of the definition but do not themselves answer the question. Understanding this helps you evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of indication
Find where the author defines mutabaqa (direct correspondence) and tadammun (inclusion). Note that mutabaqa signifies the whole meaning directly, while tadammun signifies a part that implies the whole.
2
Determine 'occurring in the way of mahiyya'
These are terms that are part of the full definition by mutabaqa, like 'animal' and 'rational' in 'rational animal' for man. They directly indicate a constituent of the quiddity.
Such terms are called 'waqi' fi tariq ma huwa'.
3
Determine 'included in the answer'
These are terms that are implied by a definiens. For example, 'body', 'growing', 'sentient', and 'voluntarily moving' are all implied by 'animal' (since 'animal' includes these meanings by tadammun). They are called 'dakhil fi jawab ma huwa'.
4
Test the validity of a single term as an answer
Ask: Can a term like 'animal' alone be a proper answer to 'what is man?'? The author says no – only the full definition via mutabaqa (e.g., 'rational animal') is correct. A part by tadammun is insufficient.
This rule prevents confusion between complete and partial definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول: وجزء المقول في جواب ما هو؟» إن كان مذكوراً بالمطابقة يسمّى «واقعاً في طريق ماهو كالحيوان والناطق بالنسبة إلى «الحيوان الناطق» المقول في جواب السؤال بما هو عن الإنسان، وإن كان مذكوراً بالتضمن يسمّى «داخلاً في جواب ماهو كالجسم والنامي والحسّاس والمتحرك بالإرادة - الدال عليها «الحيوان» بالتضمن. أقول : المقول في جواب ماهو هو الدال على الماهية المسؤل عنها بالمطابقة ، كما إذا سئل عن الإنسان بـ «ما هو ؟» فأجيب بـ «الحيوان الناطق» فإنه يدلّ على ماهية الإنسان مطابقة.
Statement: 'And a part of what is said in answer to 'what is it?'' If it is mentioned by mutabaqa (direct correspondence), it is called 'occurring in the way of mahiyya', like 'animal' and 'rational' in relation to 'rational animal' said in answer to the question 'what is it?' about man. If it is mentioned by tadammun (inclusion), it is called 'included in the answer to mahiyya', like 'body', 'growing', 'sentient', and 'voluntarily moving' which 'animal' indicates by inclusion. I say: What is said in answer to 'what is it?' is that which indicates the quiddity asked about by mutabaqa, as if one asks about man with 'what is it?' and answers with 'rational animal', for it indicates man's quiddity by mutabaqa.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a definitional classification concerning the terms used in response to the question 'what is it?' (ma huwa?), which seeks the essence of a thing. The author distinguishes two ways a term can be part of the answer: by direct correspondence (mutabaqa) or by inclusion (tadammun). If the term directly corresponds to the quiddity (mahiyya) as a whole, it is called 'occurring in the way of mahiyya' (waqi' fi tariq ma huwa). For example, 'animal' and 'rational' are parts of the complete definition 'rational animal' that directly indicates the essence of man. If the term is a part that implies the whole by inclusion, it is called 'included in the answer to mahiyya' (dakhil fi jawab ma huwa). For example, 'body', 'growing', 'sentient', and 'voluntarily moving' are each implied by the term 'animal' (since 'animal' includes these as parts). The author then clarifies that the proper answer to 'what is it?' must be by direct correspondence (mutabaqa) to accurately express the quiddity. This is because answering by inclusion or commitment (iltizam) might lead to ambiguity or incomplete understanding.

Key Terms
المطابقة
التضمن
واقع في طريق ماهو
داخل في جواب ماهو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Rational animal' (al-hayawan al-natiq)
B) 'Animal' (al-hayawan)
C) 'Man' (al-insan)
D) 'Body' (al-jism)

Key Takeaway
The answer to 'what is it?' must be by direct correspondence (mutabaqa); terms that are included (tadammun) are parts but not the whole answer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Parts of the Answer: Congruence vs Inclusion in Definition
Author explains distinction between parts mentioned by congruence vs inclusion in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between parts mentioned by congruence and parts mentioned by inclusion in the answer to 'What is it?' and explain why implication is excluded.

Core Idea
In defining essences, only congruent and inclusive terms are safe; implicative terms risk losing the intended meaning.

In classical logic, answering 'What is it?' requires precision. Not every term that relates to the essence is permitted; convention restricts us to expressions that indicate the essence directly or by inclusion, avoiding implication. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule, a cornerstone of sound definition.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three types of signification
Review mutabaqa (congruence), tadammun (inclusion), and iltizam (implication). Understand that these are the ways a word can indicate its meaning.
This classification is standard in Arabic semantics.
2
Identify the two allowed types in the answer
The passage states that parts in the answer to 'What is it?' are either 'occurring in the way of whatness' (by congruence) or 'entering into the answer' (by inclusion). Notice the different terminology.
Implication is rejected for the whole and for parts.
3
Trace the reasoning for excluding implication
Implication could lead the mind to unintended concomitants, and relying on context (qarina) is risky because it might be hidden from the listener. Therefore, convention forbids it in the essential answer.
This is a precautionary measure to ensure clarity.
4
Apply the classification to an example
Take 'man is rational animal'. The term 'animal' indicates the animal-part congruently. Within 'animal', the concept 'sensitive body' is included (tadammun). Map these to the two categories.
Both 'animal' and 'rational' are congruent for their respective parts.
5
Contrast with definitions in general
In broader definitions (ta'rifat), some scholars allow implication if context is clear, but for the essential answer to 'What is it?' the strict rule holds.
The author notes the preferable view is permissibility with clear context.

مباحث الكلي والجزئي وأما جزؤه فإن كان مذكوراً في جواب «ماهو ؟ » بالمطابقة – أي بلفظ يدلّ عليه بالمطابقة - يسمّى «واقعاً في طريق ما هو كالحيوان أو الناطق، فإن معنى «الحيوان» جزء مجموع معنى الحيوان» و«الناطق» المقول في جواب السؤال بـ «ماهو ؟ » عن الإنسان، وهو مذكور بلفظ «الحيوان» الدال عليه مطابقة.

هو طريق ما هو، وهو واقع فيه.
المقصود، وكذا ربما انتقل الذهن من الدال بالالتزام عليها إلى لازم آخر له فيفوت المقصود؛ ولا يعتمد في فهم المقصود على القرينة لجواز خفائها على السامع، وهذا المقدار كان باعثاً على الاصطلاح على أن لا تذكر الماهية في جواب «ماهو ؟» إلا بلفظ دال عليها مطابقة.
وأما جزء المقول في جواب ما هو ؟» فذلك لا يتصور إلا إذا كانت الماهية المسؤل عنها مرتبة، فيجوز أن يدلّ عليه مطابقة - وهو ظاهر - وأن يدل عليه تضمّناً ولا محذور فيه، لأن جميع الأجزاء مقصودة. ولا يجوز أن يدلّ عليه التزاماً لجواز الانتقال من ذلك الدال عن الجزء بالالتزام إلى لازم أخر له ولا يعتمد على القرينة لما عرفت. فظهر أن المطابقة معتبرة في جواب «ماهو ؟» كلاً وجزء، وأن التضمن مهجور كلاً ومعتبر جزء، وأن الالتزام مهجور كلاً وجزء، وهذا في جواب «ماهو ؟». وأما التعريفات فقد قيل أن الالتزام مهجور فيها أيضاً كما في جواب «ما هو ؟» وذلك أيضاً للاحتياط فيها والأولى جوازه فيها مع ظهور القرينة المعينة للمقصود (شريف).

وإن كان مذكوراً في جواب ماهو ؟» بالتضمّن - أي بلفظ يدلّ عليه بالتضمّن - يسمّى داخلاً في جواب ماهو»، كمفهوم الجسم النامي أو الحساس أو المتحرك بالإرادة، فإنّه جزء معنى الحيوان الناطق» المقول في جواب ماهو ؟» وهو مذكور فيه بلفظ «الحيوان» الدال عليه بالتضمّن. وإنما انحصر جزء المقول في جواب ماهو في القسمين، لأن دلالة الالتزام مهجورة في جواب «ماهو ؟ » بمعنى أنه لا يذكر في جواب «ماهو ؟» لفظ يدل على الماهية المسؤل عنها أو على أجزائها بالالتزام اصطلاحاً.
Discussion of the universal and particular. As for its part: if it is mentioned in the answer to 'What is it?' by congruence – i.e., by a word that indicates it by congruence – it is called 'occurring in the way of whatness', like 'animal' or 'rational', for the meaning of 'animal' is a part of the total meaning of 'animal' and 'rational' said in answer to the question 'What is it?' concerning man, and it is mentioned with the word 'animal' that indicates it congruently. It is called 'occurring in the way of whatness' because what is said in answer to 'What is it?' is the way of whatness, and it occurs therein. The intended meaning; similarly, the mind might transfer from the signifier by implication to another necessary concomitant of it, and the intended meaning is missed; and one does not rely on context to understand the intended meaning because it might be hidden from the listener. This amount was the motive for the convention that the essence is not mentioned in answer to 'What is it?' except by a word that indicates it congruently. As for the part of what is said in answer to 'What is it?', that is only conceivable if the essence asked about is composed; then it is permissible to indicate it congruently – which is obvious – and to indicate it by inclusion without harm, because all parts are intended. It is not permissible to indicate it by implication, because of the possibility of transferring from that signifier of the part by implication to another necessary concomitant of it, and one does not rely on context for what you know. So it appears that congruence is valid in the answer to 'What is it?' both as a whole and as a part; inclusion is rejected as a whole but valid as a part; and implication is rejected both as a whole and as a part. This is for the answer to 'What is it?'. As for definitions, it is said that implication is also rejected in them as in the answer to 'What is it?', and that is also for caution; but the preferable view is its permissibility in them with the appearance of context indicating the intended meaning (Sharif). (1) Specifying 'occurring in the way' for the part indicated congruently and specifying 'entering into the answer' for the part indicated by inclusion is a convention, and the appropriateness in naming is observed. And if it is mentioned in the answer to 'What is it?' by inclusion – i.e., by a word that indicates it by inclusion – it is called 'entering into the answer to What is it?', like the concept of growing body, or sensitive, or moving by will; for it is a part of the meaning of 'rational animal' said in answer to 'What is it?', and it is mentioned therein with the word 'animal' indicating it by inclusion. And the part of what is said in answer to 'What is it?' is limited to these two divisions because the implication is rejected in the answer to 'What is it?' in the sense that no word is mentioned in answer to 'What is it?' that indicates the essence asked about or its parts by implication, as a convention.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage defines the two types of parts that can occur in the answer to the question 'What is it?' (the quiddity question). The author explains that if a part is mentioned by مطابقة (congruence), it is called 'occurring in the way of whatness' (واقع في طريق ما هو). For example, in answering 'What is man?', the term 'animal' is a congruent expression for the animal part of man. The rationale is that the answer to 'What is it?' is supposed to give the essence directly, and implication (التزام) could lead the mind to unintended meanings, so only congruence and inclusion are allowed. Inclusion (تضمن) is permissible for parts but not for the whole; for example, 'animal' in 'rational animal' includes the concept of 'sensitive body' by inclusion. The passage stresses that implication is avoided entirely in the answer to 'What is it?' due to the risk of ambiguity, though in wider definitions (التعريفات) it may be allowed with clear context. This establishes a foundational convention in logic for defining essences.

التزام
واقع في طريق ما هو
داخل في جواب ما هو

In the answer to 'What is it?', only congruent and inclusive terms are allowed for parts; implication is strictly avoided to prevent ambiguity, though in broader definitions it may be permitted with clear context.

The Differentia: Constitutive to Species, Divisive to Genus
Author explains how differentia relates to species (constitutive) and genus (divisive), and rules for each level.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two relations of the differentia (constitutive and divisive) and apply the rules for highest genus, lowest species, and intermediates to determine whether a given differentia is constitutive, divisive, or both.

Core Idea
The differentia constitutes the species but divides the genus – one term, two opposite logical functions.

The differentia (الفصل) is one of the five universals, but it has a dual nature. When attached to the species, it is a part of its essence; when attached to the genus, it splits the genus into subdivisions. This passage from Qutb al-Din al-Razi's commentary explains these two relations and gives rules for how the differentia behaves at different levels of generality – from the highest genus down to the lowest species.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two relations of the differentia
The author states: 'The differentia has a relation to the species and a relation to the genus.' Identify which relation is constitutive (مقوم) and which is divisive (مقسم). The first makes the differentia part of the species' essence; the second splits the genus into species.
Remember: 'constitutive' is internal to the species, 'divisive' is external to the genus.
2
Apply the example: 'rational' with 'human' and 'animal'
See how 'rational' constitutes 'human' (it is part of the definition of human) but divides 'animal' (it combines with 'animal' to form 'rational animal', a species of animal). Explain why 'rational' does not constitute 'animal'.
The same differentia plays different roles depending on what it is attached to.
3
Analyze the rules for highest genus, lowest species, and intermediates
The text says: the highest genus may have a constitutive differentia and must have a divisive one; the lowest species must have a constitutive differentia and cannot have a divisive one; intermediates must have both. For each level, determine why these rules hold based on the definitions of 'highest' and 'lowest'.
The highest genus has no genus above it, so it can be composed of coequal matters. The lowest species has no species below it, so no division is needed.
4
Examine the transitivity rules
The author states: 'Every differentia that constitutes the highest constitutes the lowest without universal converse, and every differentia that divides the lowest divides the highest without converse.' Understand that if a differentia is part of the essence of a highest genus, it automatically becomes part of all lower species. Conversely, if a differentia distinguishes a lowest species, it also divides all higher genera.
This is a key principle for transferring differentiae across levels of generality.
5
Clarify the misconception about division into two
The marginal note explains that 'rational' does not divide 'animal' into two halves; it only produces one division ('rational animal'). The opposite division ('non-rational animal') arises from the absence of rationality, not from the differentia itself. Thus, each differentia produces only one division.
This nuance prevents a logical error: the differentia is not responsible for both sides of the division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٦- نسبة الفصل إلى النوع والجنس]
قال : والجنس العالي جاز أن يكون له فصل يقومه، لجواز تركيبه من أمرين متساويين أو أمور متساوية ويجب أن يكون له فصل يقسمه. والنوع السافل يجب أن يكون له فصل يقومه ويمتنع أن يكون له فصل يقسمه.
والمتوسطات يجب أن يكون لها فصول تقسمها وفصول تقومها وكل فصل يقوم العالي فهو يقوم السافل من غير عكس كلي، وكل فصل يقسم السافل فهو يقسم العالي من غير عكس.
القول : الفصل له نسبة إلى النوع ونسبة إلى الجنس – أي جنس ذلك النوع -
فأما نسبته إلى النوع : فبأنه مقوم له - أي داخل في قوامه وجزء له.
وأما نسبته إلى الجنس : فإنه مقسم له - أي محصل قسم له - فإنه إذا انضم إلى الجنس صار المجموع قسماً من الجنس ونوعاً له، مثلاً «الناطق» إذا نسب إلى «الإنسان» فهو داخل في قوامه وماهيته، وإذا نسب إلى «الحيوان» صار حيواناً ناطقاً، وهو قسم من الحيوان.
إذا تصورت هذا فنقول :
الجنس العالي جاز أن يكون له فصل يقومه، لجواز أن يتركب من أمرين متساويين يساويانه ويميزانه عن مشاركاته في الوجود، وقد امتنع القدماء عن ذلك بناء على أن كل ماهية لها فصل يقومها لابد أن يكون لها جنس - وقد سلف ذلك -
ويجب أن يكون له - أي للجنس العالي - فصل يقسمه، لوجوب أن يكون تحته أنواع وفصول الأنواع بالقياس إلى الجنس مقسمات له.
(۱) قد يتوهم أن الناطق - مثلاً - يقسم الحيوان إلى قسمين ناطق وغير ناطق، والتحقيق أنه مقسم له بمعنى أنه محصل قسم له، لا محصل قسمين؛ فإن غير الناطق قسم من الحيوان حاصل من انضمام عدم النطق إليه، كما أن الناطق قسم منه حاصل بانضمام النطق إليه، فإذا قسم الحيوان إلى هذين القسمين كان هناك أمران مقسمان له كل واحد منهما محصل قسم واحد له. وكان من قال إن الناطق يقسم الحيوان إلى قسمين» نظر إلى أن الحيوان إذا قيس إلى الناطق وجوداً وعدماً حصل له قسمان، كما أن من عد المفرد من الأنواع والأجناس في المراتب نظر إلى مثل ذلك (شريف).
36- The Relation of the Differentia to the Species and the Genus]
He said: The highest genus may have a differentia that constitutes it, because it may be composed of two coequal matters or coequal matters, and it must have a differentia that divides it. The lowest species must have a differentia that constitutes it, and it is impossible for it to have a differentia that divides it. The intermediate (categories) must have differentiae that divide them and differentiae that constitute them. Every differentia that constitutes the highest constitutes the lowest without universal converse, and every differentia that divides the lowest divides the highest without converse.
The statement: The differentia has a relation to the species and a relation to the genus – i.e., the genus of that species.
As for its relation to the species: it is constitutive of it – i.e., entering into its constitution and a part of it.
As for its relation to the genus: it is divisive of it – i.e., a producer of a division of it. For when it joins the genus, the combination becomes a division of the genus and a species of it. For example, 'rational' when related to 'human' is part of its constitution and quiddity, and when related to 'animal' becomes a rational animal, which is a division of animal.
If you understand this, we say:
The highest genus may have a differentia that constitutes it, because it may be composed of two coequal matters that equal it and distinguish it from its partners in existence. The ancients prevented/denied that, based on the fact that every quiddity that has a differentia constituting it must have a genus – and that has preceded.
And it must have – i.e., the highest genus – a differentia that divides it, because it is necessary that there be under it species, and the differentiae of species in relation to the genus are divisions of it.
(1) One might imagine that 'rational' – for example – divides animal into two divisions: rational and non-rational. But the verification is that it is a divider in the sense that it is a producer of one division of it, not a producer of two divisions. For the non-rational is a division of animal resulting from the joining of the absence of rationality to it, just as the rational is a division of it resulting from the joining of rationality to it. When animal is divided into these two divisions, there are two things dividing it, each one of them producing one division of it. And whoever said that the rational divides animal into two divisions considered that when animal is measured against rationality in terms of existence and non-existence, it acquires two divisions, just as whoever counted the single [differentia] among the species and genera in the ranks considered something similar (Sharif).
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines the relationship of the differentia (الفصل) to the species (النوع) and the genus (الجنس). It is a definitional passage that clarifies the logical roles of the differentia. The author begins by stating that the differentia has two relations: to the species, it is constitutive (مقوم), meaning it enters into the essence of the species; to the genus, it is divisive (مقسم), meaning it produces a subdivision of the genus. An example is given: 'rational' (ناطق) when related to 'human' is part of its quiddity, but when related to 'animal' it yields 'rational animal', a division of animal. The passage then applies this to the categories of genera and species. The highest genus (الجنس العالي) may have a constitutive differentia because it could be composed of two coequal matters, but it must have a divisive differentia to allow for species beneath it. The lowest species (النوع السافل) must have a constitutive differentia but cannot have a divisive one because it has no species beneath it. Intermediate categories must have both. Additionally, a constitutive differentia of the highest genus also constitutes all lower species, but not vice versa; a divisive differentia of the lowest species also divides all higher genera, but not vice versa. The author then notes that some early scholars rejected the idea that the highest genus can have a constitutive differentia, arguing that every quiddity with a constitutive differentia must have a genus, which the highest genus lacks. Finally, a clarification is given in the marginal note: the differentia does not divide the genus into two exact halves; rather, it produces one division, and the opposite division results from the absence of the differentia.

Key Terms

جنس
نوع
مقوم
مقسم

A) It must have a constitutive differentia and may have a divisive differentia.
B) It must have a constitutive differentia and cannot have a divisive differentia.
C) It may have a constitutive differentia and must have a divisive differentia.
D) It cannot have either a constitutive or a divisive differentia.

Key Takeaway
The differentia has two distinct logical relations: it constitutes the species (as part of its essence) and divides the genus (by producing a species), with specific rules depending on the level of generality.

Conditions of the Definer (al-Mu'arraf)
Author defines al-mu'arraf and states three invalid possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid definer (al-mu'arraf) and test whether a given expression fulfills them.

Core Idea
A definer must be equal in generality to the defined—not identical, broader, or narrower.

This lesson examines the foundational conditions for a valid definer in Islamic logic. The definer (al-mu'arraf) is that which, when conceived, leads to the conception and distinction of the defined. The matn lays out three invalid possibilities, leaving us with the necessary condition: equality in generality and particularity. Understanding these conditions is essential for evaluating definitions in any Islamic science, from fiqh to kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definer's function
Find the definition of al-mu'arraf: it is that whose conception necessitates the conception of the thing being defined and its distinction from everything else. Note the two requirements: conception and distinction.
2
List the three prohibited categories
The matn states three things the definer cannot be: (1) the essence itself, (2) more general, (3) more specific. Write them down in order.
3
Understand why each is prohibited
For each category, see the reason given: (1) ya'rif (definer) must be known before the defined, but the essence cannot be known before itself; (2) more general is insufficient to single out the defined; (3) more specific is more obscure and fails to clarify.
The reasons are based on the purpose of definition: to make something known.
4
Conclude the necessary equality
Since the above three are invalid, the definer must be equal (musāwī) to the defined in generality and particularity. This is the logical conclusion of the matn.
Equality here means coextensive: every instance of the definer is an instance of the defined and vice versa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال :
الفصل الرابع
في التعريفات
المعرف للشيء - وهو الذي يستلزم تصوّره تصور ذلك الشيء وامتيازه عن كل ماعداه - وهو لا يجوز أن يكون نفس الماهية، لأن المعرف معلوم قبل المعرف، والشيء لا يعلم قبل نفسه.
ولا اعم لقصوره عن إفادة التعريف.
ولا أخص لكونه أخفي.
فهو مساو لها في العموم والخصوص.
أقول : قد سلف لك أنّ نظر المنطقي إما في القول الشارح أو في الحجة، ولكلّ منهما مقدمات يتوقف معرفته عليها؛ ولما وقع الفراغ من بيان مقدمات القول الشارح فقد حان أن يشرع فيه :
فالقول الشارح هو المعرف)، وهو ما يستلزم تصوره تصور الشيء
(1) أعني مايكون تصوّره بطريق النظر موصلاً إلى تصوّر الشيء أو امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه، وهذا القيد يفهم اعتباره لما تقدّم من أن الموصل بالنظر إلى التصور يسمى «قولاً شارحاً».
He said: The fourth chapter on definitions. The definer of a thing—and it is that whose conception necessitates the conception of that thing and its distinction from everything else—and it is not permissible for it to be the essence itself, because the definer is known before the defined, and a thing is not known before itself. Nor more general, due to its insufficiency to convey the definition. Nor more specific, because it would be more obscure. So it is equal to it in generality and particularity. I say: It has already preceded you that the logician's consideration is either in the expository statement (qawl sharḥ) or in the argument, and each has premises upon which knowledge of it depends. And when the clarification of the premises of the expository statement has been completed, it is time to commence it. So the expository statement is the definer—that whose conception, by way of theoretical examination, leads to the conception of the thing or its distinction from everything else. And this condition is understood to be considered due to what preceded: that that which conveys by theoretical examination to conception is called an 'expository statement'.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage opens the fourth chapter on definitions (al-ta'rīfāt). First, the matn (original text) defines the definer (al-mu'arraf): it is that whose conception (taṣawwur) necessitates the conception of the thing being defined and its distinction from all others. It then states three things it cannot be: (1) the essence itself, because the definer must be known before the defined and a thing cannot be known before itself; (2) more general, because it would be too broad to specify the defined; (3) more specific, because it would be more obscure and thus ineffective. Therefore, it must be equal in generality and particularity to the defined. The commentator (the author of the sharḥ) then adds that the logician's concern is either with the expository statement (qawl sharḥ) or with the argument (ḥujja). After finishing the premises for the expository statement, now it is time to discuss it. The expository statement is the definer, and it is that which, through theoretical investigation, leads to the conception of the thing or its distinction from others. This is consistent with the earlier statement that the term 'qawl sharḥ' applies to whatever conveys conception through theoretical means.

Key Terms
المعرف
قول شارح
ماهية
تساو

A) It must be equal to the defined in generality and particularity.
B) It can be the essence itself.
C) It must necessitate the conception and distinction of the defined.
D) It cannot be more general.

Key Takeaway
The definer must be coextensive with the defined—neither identical, nor broader, nor narrower.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Definiens: Its Definition and Conditions
Author defines the definiens and states its conditions of not being essence, broader, or narrower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the definiens and list the three conditions that it cannot be the essence, broader, or narrower than the definiendum.

Core Idea
The definiens must be coextensive with the definiendum to properly define it.

In Islamic logic, a valid definition requires a definiens that precisely matches the definiendum. This lesson introduces the definition of 'definiens' (al-mu'arraf) and its essential negative conditions, as laid down by Qutb al-Din al-Razi. Understanding these conditions is crucial for evaluating definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Find the definition of definiens
Read the opening Arabic sentence. The definiens is defined as 'that whose conception necessitates the conception of the thing and its distinction from all others.' Identify this definition.
2
Identify the first condition: not essence
The text says it cannot be the same as the essence (māhiyya). Why? Because the definiens is known before the definiendum, and a thing cannot be known before itself.
3
Identify the second condition: not broader
The definiens cannot be broader (a'am) than the definiendum because it would fail to specify the thing adequately.
4
Identify the third condition: not narrower
The definiens cannot be narrower (akhass) because it would be more obscure than the definiendum.
5
Conclude: must be coextensive
Therefore, the definiens must be equal (musāwī) in generality and specificity to the definiendum.
This is the logical requirement for a real definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الرابع في التعريفات المعرف للشيء - وهو الذي يستلزم تصوّره تصور ذلك الشيء وامتيازه عن كل ماعداه - وهو لا يجوز أن يكون نفس الماهية، لأن المعرف معلوم قبل المعرّف، والشيء لا يعلم قبل نفسه. ولا اعم لقصوره عن إفادة التعريف. ولا أخص لكونه أخفي. فهو مساو لها في العموم والخصوص. أقول : قد سلف لك أنّ نظر المنطقي إما في القول الشارح أو في الحجة، ولكلّ منهما مقدمات يتوقف معرفته عليها؛ ولما وقع الفراغ من بيان مقدمات القول الشارح فقد حان أن يشرع فيه: فالقول الشارح هو المعرف)، وهو ما يستلزم تصوره تصور الشيء أعني مايكون تصوّره بطريق النظر موصلاً إلى تصوّر الشيء أو امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه، وهذا القيد يفهم اعتباره لما تقدّم من أن الموصل بالنظر إلى التصور يسمى «قولاً شارحاً». أو امتيازه عن كل ماعداه؛ وليس المراد بتصوّر الشيء تصوّره بوجه ما، والا لكان الأعم من الشيء أو الأخص منه معرفا له - لأنه قد يستلزم [؟] وكيف لا يكون معتبراً والمقصود من الفن بيان طرق اكتساب التصورات والتصديقات، ومع هذا القيد لانقض بأن تصور المعرف يستلزم أيضاً تصور معرفه، فينتقض حد المعرف به، ولا بأن تصوّر الماهيات يستلزم تصوّر لوازمها البينة المعتبرة في دلالة الالتزام، إذ ليس شيء من هذين الاستلزامين بطريق النظر والاكتساب (شريف).
Chapter Four on Definitions. The definiens of a thing – and it is that whose conception necessitates the conception of that thing and its distinction from everything other than it – and it is not permissible for it to be the same as the essence, because the definiens is known before the definiendum, and a thing is not known before itself. Nor broader, due to its deficiency in providing definition. Nor narrower, due to it being more obscure. So it is equal to it in generality and specificity. I say: it has preceded to you that the logician's consideration is either in the clarifying statement or in the proof, and each of them has premises upon which knowledge of it depends; and when the explanation of the premises of the clarifying statement is finished, it is time to begin it. So the clarifying statement is the definiens, and it is that whose conception necessitates the conception of the thing – I mean, whose conception by way of inference leads to the conception of the thing or its distinction from all others. And this restriction is understood to be considered due to what has preceded: that that which leads by inference to conception is called 'clarifying statement'. Or distinction from everything else. And what is intended by the conception of the thing is not its conception in any respect, for then the broader or the narrower of the thing would be a definiens for it – because it may necessitate [؟]. And how could it not be considered? And the purpose of the discipline is to explain the ways of acquiring conceptions and assents. And with this restriction, it is not refuted that the conception of the definiens also necessitates the conception of its definiendum, for then the definition of the definiens would be refuted by it; nor that the conception of essences necessitates the conception of their obvious concomitants considered in implicative signification, for neither of these two necessities is by way of inference and acquisition.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a definitional passage that defines the definiens (al-mu'arraf) and specifies its essential conditions. It begins by stating the definition: the definiens is that whose conception necessitates the conception of the thing and its distinction from all others. The author then explains three negative conditions: (1) It cannot be the essence itself, because the definiens is known before the definiendum. (2) It cannot be broader (more general), because it would fail to adequately specify the thing. (3) It cannot be narrower (more specific), because it would be more obscure than the definiendum. Therefore, it must be coextensive (musawi) in generality and specificity. The commentator then expands on this, explaining that the clarifying statement (al-qawl al-sharih) is the definiens, and emphasizes that the conception must be by way of inference (bi-tariq al-nazar), not just any conception. He addresses two potential objections to the condition that the definiens must lead to conception through inference: (a) The conception of the definiens itself would require another definition, but this implication is not by inference. (b) The conception of an essence necessarily implies its obvious concomitants, but this implication is also not by inference. Thus the definition remains sound.

Key Terms
المعرف
القول الشارح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why cannot the definiens be broader (a'am) than the definiendum?
A) Because it would be more obscure
B) Because it would fail to provide adequate definition (qusur 'an ifadat al-ta'rif)
C) Because it would be the same as the essence
D) Because it would require prior knowledge of the definiens

Key Takeaway
The definiens cannot be identical to the essence, nor broader, nor narrower; it must be coextensive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Check the following definition of 'gharar' (uncertainty): 'a transaction where the outcome is unknown.' Is this a valid definiens? Which condition does it violate?
?
Provide a fiqh example where a broader definiens would lead to an incorrect ruling.
